        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219428403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14112747581686314368">Reread.........loved it just as much as I did when I first put my hands on this book!!!<br/><br/>Original review:<br/><blockquote>
  <b>”Somewhere in the universe, two hearts reached out and connected.</b>
</blockquote><br/>Opening line…<blockquote>
  <b>When you're eighteen, there's fuck-all to do in a Southern Illinois summer but eat fried pickles, drink PBR tallboys you stole from your mom, and ride the Tilt-a-Whirl till you hurl. Which is exactly what I was doing the night I met Him. </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909905.gif' alt=' photo 45895-sheldon-mind-blown-gif-FLgC_zps5tdc6hen.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This is the best book I have read in 2015!!!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909906.gif' alt=' photo giphy_zpsste4srby.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>It wasn’t just the fantastic </span>
  <span id="freeText14112747581686314368" style="display:none">Reread.........loved it just as much as I did when I first put my hands on this book!!!<br><br>Original review:<br><blockquote>
  <b>”Somewhere in the universe, two hearts reached out and connected.</b>
</blockquote><br>Opening line…<blockquote>
  <b>When you're eighteen, there's fuck-all to do in a Southern Illinois summer but eat fried pickles, drink PBR tallboys you stole from your mom, and ride the Tilt-a-Whirl till you hurl. Which is exactly what I was doing the night I met Him. </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909905.gif" alt=" photo 45895-sheldon-mind-blown-gif-FLgC_zps5tdc6hen.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is the best book I have read in 2015!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909906.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zpsste4srby.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It wasn’t just the fantastic storyline…..the love affair between a teacher and a student….<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909907.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_miahd8n0kZ1s5rmrwo1_500_zpsdymqz3nj.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">… it wasn’t just the incredible first pages…<blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425593807i/13909908.jpg" alt=" photo 864125_zps2q8epbkq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote> , it wasn’t just the most beautiful , the most lyrical writing ever…<blockquote><b>”and that made my heart ache, too. The thought of how much happiness lay scattered across the universe, unrealized in fragments, waiting for the right twist of fate to bring it together.”</b></blockquote>, it wasn’t just the intense chemistry, passion and emotional connection between Maisie &amp; Evan…<br>Evan telling Maisie <blockquote><b>”You’re the first. You’re the first of so many things.”</b></blockquote> <br>and Maisie…..<blockquote><b>”The world is new when I’m with you.”</b></blockquote>…..<br><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425593807i/13909909.jpg" alt=" photo 1407556c1bfc9d503a3b4c90ceda0405_zpstxg4xbmk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote><br>it’s all those things that have stayed with me ….but most of all, what made this book UNFORGETABLE for me, was Maisie!!! Evan was so right when he said….<blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425593807i/13909910.jpg" alt=" photo 462436_1276101556492_full_zpszesz6ppg.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote><br>What an incredible and compelling and admirable character. There was so much about her that I loved. The sad and horrible upbringing she has endured doesn’t stop her from following her dreams. She goes after what she wants. She’s strong; she’s honest and not afraid to own up to her actions.<br><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425593807i/13909911.jpg" alt=" photo 11d7110c5c49d622ab8af1b43c1e2d23_zpscmwp1avt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote> Mature and at the same time naive. A compelling journey of a young and broken girl finding herself. <br><br><b>"I can't hold on to you. You're like that shooting star. Just a trail of fire in my hands."</b><br>I connected with her and loved seeing her trying to find herself and what she wanted to do with her life.<br><br>I so wanted things to work out for Maisie &amp; Evan…I had to hold myself back from sneaking a peep at the last page….<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425593807ra/13909912.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_njzjs2TMKz1r702nz_zpsvffrpfvs.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>…well, the ending was totally unexpected!!!! But I was happy how the story wrapped up….<br><br>This is a book that will stay with me for a very long time and it’s one of those that I will definitely read again and again.<br><br>I can’t recommend this book enough for anyone who loves a beautifully written love story.<br><br>It’s incredible that this is the author’s debut novel!! I can’t wait to read more by her.</span>

<div id="review_1624948482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1624948482" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1624948482?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1624948482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11110746631459640127">All I can say is that I was so into the story that I forgot to take notes, wow.<br/>This story was not at all what I was expecting, though a bit melodramatic towards the end.<br/><br/>Also, Siobhan was incredibly wonderful, I’m really glad Maise connected with her.<br/><br/><i>“I am not the wise woman you think,” she said, tilting her glass. Starlight skimmed off the rim and shot into her eyes, sparkling. “But I will tell you this: don’t put your life on hold for someone, or you’ll wake up at forty-two with an empty house </i></span>
  <span id="freeText11110746631459640127" style="display:none">All I can say is that I was so into the story that I forgot to take notes, wow.<br>This story was not at all what I was expecting, though a bit melodramatic towards the end.<br><br>Also, Siobhan was incredibly wonderful, I’m really glad Maise connected with her.<br><br><i>“I am not the wise woman you think,” she said, tilting her glass. Starlight skimmed off the rim and shot into her eyes, sparkling. “But I will tell you this: don’t put your life on hold for someone, or you’ll wake up at forty-two with an empty house and a terrifying sense of freedom and no energy or innocence left to enjoy it.”</i><br><br><b>*Spoilers below*</b>:<br><br>But I was kind of disappointed when Maise went back to Evan after Wesley showed his Docudrama about her life and everyone in class started discussing it, I realized how wrong their relationship was in my eyes and how I couldn’t stand her being with him. We’d been in Maise’s head for so long, it was easy to forget the wrongness. But Wesley’s Docudrama showed me how it looked from an outsider’s perspective. I was in such a haze, just like Maise, and it was like finally waking up after I saw it.<br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1516695153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1516695153" />
    <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth"><img alt="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487525094p2/13870608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1516695153?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth">Jo ★The Book Sloth★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=na">na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=time-waste">time-waste</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=insta-love-lust">insta-love-lust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1516695153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9979655789119347870"><b>1 You're a Statistic Waiting to Happen Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453491890i/17835032.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Unteachable revolves around a girl, a young woman really, raised in poverty by a highly inadequate mother, in conditions no child should ever witness, much less face every day. But Unteachable isn't a life story, it is a love story, even better, it is a "forbidden love" story, and as most "forbidden love" stories, it starts with a glance that leads to a night that should have never happened. It speaks about the romance that develops between this too-ja</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9979655789119347870" style="display:none"><b>1 You're a Statistic Waiting to Happen Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453491890i/17835032.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Unteachable revolves around a girl, a young woman really, raised in poverty by a highly inadequate mother, in conditions no child should ever witness, much less face every day. But Unteachable isn't a life story, it is a love story, even better, it is a "forbidden love" story, and as most "forbidden love" stories, it starts with a glance that leads to a night that should have never happened. It speaks about the romance that develops between this too-jaded for her years girl and her high-school teacher and how that romance affects their already screwed-up life. How one bad choice leads to more bad choices to wrong decisions to twisted situations to a fucked up year. Can love survive so many wrong turns?</i><br><br><b>
  <u>UNTAGGED SPOILERS APLENTY</u>
</b><br><br>I had a weird sense of deja vu with the beginning of this book. The whole "one-night-stand turns out to be my teacher" thing has been done by Pretty Litte Liars(the series, I haven't read the books) much better IMO. Unteachable was the equivalent of the train wreck for me. How can you like absolutely nothing about a book and still feel compelled to finish it, to see how things work out? And I honestly didn't like anything about the book. I didn't like the characters, I didn't like the writing, I didn't like the romance and I definitely didn't like the ending.<br><br><b>
  <u>The writing</u>
</b><br><br>The writing was... I can barely find the words to describe the writing. I guess it was way too poetic for my taste. The whole book read like a fucking dream-scene. Too many metaphors and comparisons, too many "stars in eyes" and "inflating heart"s and "breaths suspended in limbo"s, or whatever version of those the author used, for my liking. Some people(most people it would seem) find it beautiful. To me it was just tiring and annoying and made me want to quit 25% in the book. To quote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7105371.Leah_Raeder" rel="nofollow noopener">the author</a>, obviousy "pretendiously lyrical fiction" doesn't agree with me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453492012i/17835042.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Prime example of the shit spewed every other sentence.</i><br><br><b>
  <u>The Romance</u>
</b><br><br>The love story was shallow at best, obsessive at worst. For the most part it was sex-based, since more than half of the book that was all Maise and Evan did, have sex that is. After that half, it becomes obvious that Maise has fallen in obsession with Evan. Everything except Evan is a blur in her mind. School, her "friends", her mother, all has become irrelevant and the only hours she "lives" are the hours spent with her crush. And it is a crush, because how can you love someone you know next to nothing about? For about 70% of the book Maise has to literally drag any tidbit of info about Evan out of him. After the 70% point, everything Maise learns isn't positive since it points to the fact that what she has with Evan is based on lies, omitions and half-truths. So...where exactly is the love there? And if your love is one that has to be kept a secret from everyone, one that you have to lie about every day, can it survive in the light? When the thrill of hiding, a thrill that was one of the things that excited them, wears off is there anything left behind? I honestly don't know.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That was what we'd finally been forced to confront: if our relationship was based on forbiddenness, what would happen when it was no longer forbidden?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <u>Maise</u>
</b><br><br>What a stuck-up, self-righteous bitch. Maise could, and should, have been a heroine I could root for. A heroine I would want to see succeeding and having everything life owed her, and life did owe her, BIG! Beeing born to a junkie/dealer/prostitute mother who gave no shit about her was bound to be tough. Said mother being your only relative, even worse. I can literally not even imagine how much this can twist a person. This however does not mean that I have to approve of her or her shitty choices just because she had it bad. So, without further ado, Maise's screw ups...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Grow up. This is real. The world is ugly and nasty and fucked up, and so are we.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>1)<i> Boys her own age are just kids and Maise is too mature and jaded for kids. She needs real men, grown up men.</i><br>I can get behind the idea that a girl with Maise's life can't have much in common with other high-school kids, but believing a whole age group, your age group, beneath you just means that you're a pretendious bitch. Especially when all you're looking for is a random hook-up not a relationship or even a real conversation. Yes, a lot can be said about experience in THAT department but, sweety, you just can't be the only "special snowflake" out there. And when she goes as far as to put down her only friend using his age, she basically crashed and burned completely for me.<br><br>2)<i> Maise won't sacrifice her future by being irresponsible in sex, so let's leave the condom behind, that shows plenty of responsibility.</i><br>Our mature and responsible heroine won't jeopardise her future by doing something as stupid as getting pregnant for no man, not even Evan, but she's on the pill, so let's go bareback. Because, as we all know in the 21st century, condoms only protect us from pregnancy. Inconsequential things like STDs and AIDS only happen to other people. So sure, don't use a ccondom with a guy you know less than a month and who, let's not forget, actually started as an one-night-stand, because you're mature and responsible like that.<br><br>3)<i> She becomes a drug dealer because, hey, "she didn't have a choice".</i><br>That's a huge NO for me. I don't care how many slaps life has given you, I don't care if Zeus himself is threatening to out your "forbidden affair". There are always choices, like going to the police, or letting your teacher/boyfriend quit his job as he should have done long ago, or hell, what she actually did in the end. Your only choice isn't providing 17-year-old girls with drugs. I wonder, if one ODed, how the hell would you live with yourself then, oh self-righteous one?<br><br>But nope... In all of this Maise is somehow better that other 18 years olds.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453492012i/17835044.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Evan</u>
</b><br><br>And here comes Evan the liar. Evan, who from the beginning supossedly wanted what he had with Maise to be "more than an one-night-stand", goes on to lie to her for half a year. He lies about his past, or at least ommits some pretty serious shit, he lies about his friend, hell, he even lies about his fucking name. This guy gets involved with a student even though he already knows exactly how bad it can get and how much it can screw over your life. He just can't resist an "adoring young fan" because that's exactly what this is about. He never even really tried to stir Maise away from a relationship that was obviously unheathy for a girl who was already too full of issues. Instead he manipulated her into secrecy by a series of suggestions that he give up his job and livelihood(not so much since he could work at another school) so they could be together openly, but never actually did it until it all came crashing around them. He even had the nerve to suggest she quit his class. A class Maise needed on her curriculum to more easily get into her school of choice. Way to show you care you asshole.<br><br>And here comes the "statistic waiting to happen" part. Since he actually admits that her age is one of the things that attracted him to her(pervert much?), I can practically see their future. In 8-15 years, when Maise won't be so young and vibrant and full of life anymore, there will be another young and adoring girl who will like "real men" and not her high-school mates. There will be another "quicky in the car" followed by a secret affair, while Maise waits at home, probably feeding their 2.4 kids and planting roses besides their white picket fence. The author herself proved my point with Wesley's perfect mom and how she dated her teacher and how, now, said teacher is going out with the new, young, 22-year-old model and she is divorced and at home raising their son.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453492012i/17835043.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I know... How about not looking for it up your students' skirts??? Just a suggestion!</i><br><br><b>
  <u>Wesley</u>
</b><br><br>STALKER ALERT!!! That's all....<br><br><b>
  <u>The Ending</u>
</b><br><br>The ending can be described with two words: TOO RUSHED! Everything was resolved so fast and neatly, it actually made my head spin. I would have preferred a bittersweet(got into school, never saw Evan again), or even a sad(had to retake exams to get into school, never saw Evan again), or even a weird(got into school, went into a relationship with Wesley) ending much more that I liked the HEA we actually got. I can't believe I'm saying this, me, the person who despises anything but a HEA, but I actually hated it this time. Everything suddenly fell into place and all the built-up, all the drama was for nothing. Suddenly there were choices and everything was right in the world. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453501872ra/17836086.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The thought of how much happiness lay scattered across the universe, unrealized, in fragments, waiting for the right twist of fate to bring it together.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book soooo wasn't the right twist for me...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9979655789119347870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_680230549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/680230549" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13247178-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473718933p2/13247178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680230549?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/13247178-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17978680-unteachable">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=hot-hot-hot">hot-hot-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=unputdownable">unputdownable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=emotional-rollercoaster">emotional-rollercoaster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680230549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3667488823744472895"><br/>♦ <i>I met him at a carnival, of all corny places...</i> ♦<p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430988ra/864497.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
</p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You can call it love. Or you can call it freefall. They're pretty much the same thing."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430988i/864498.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>For days I've been hearing nothing but very positive reactions about Leah Raeder's exquisite writing style and her NA debut novel <i>Unteachable</i>. So, of course, I had to find out for myself what everyone kept raving about. And let me tell you, it did not disappoint. The author's lyrical, prose-like writing style managed to suck me in from the </span>
  <span id="freeText3667488823744472895" style="display:none"><br>♦ <i>I met him at a carnival, of all corny places...</i> ♦<p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430988ra/864497.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
</p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You can call it love. Or you can call it freefall. They're pretty much the same thing."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430988i/864498.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For days I've been hearing nothing but very positive reactions about Leah Raeder's exquisite writing style and her NA debut novel <i>Unteachable</i>. So, of course, I had to find out for myself what everyone kept raving about. And let me tell you, it did not disappoint. The author's lyrical, prose-like writing style managed to suck me in from the moment I started reading it until the very last page.<br><br><b><i>Unteachable</i> deals with a common taboo subject: student/teacher relationship.</b><br><br>Yet, it never became predictable or clichéd in any way, which is part of the reason I ended up enjoying this story so much.<br><br><i>It all starts out on a warm summer evening...</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430988i/864499._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Maise O'Malley</b> is an eighteen year old girl with a broken past. Growing up with an absent father and an irresponsible mother has left her having to take care of herself from a young age. The lack of a loving family has left her feeling empty inside. But throughout the years, she has found her own coping mechanisms to handle this void inside her.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Thanks Dad, for leaving a huge void in my life that Freud says has to be filled with dick."</i>
</b><br><br>I immediately liked Maise's no-nonsense, sarcastic attitude. She's down to earth, doesn't care what other people think about her and she seems wise beyond her years. <br><br>Every month she tries to confront one of her fears. This time, she decides to face the fear of being on a roller coaster ride at the carnival, all by herself.<br><br>And that's where she meets Evan.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430988i/864500._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Right at the last moment he joins her on the ride that will change both of their lives for good.<br><br>*<br><br><i><b>"You're pretty brave,"</b> he said, lowering the bar over us. <b>"Must be a veteran, sitting up front."</b><br><br><b>"It's my first time,"</b> I said. Well, first time on my own terms.<br><br>He smiled. It hit his face like a camera flash. <b>"Mine too."</b></i><br><br>*<br><br>And so it begins...<br><br>Their one night of fun, passion and carelessness..<br><br>A night that ends in the backseat of a car.<br><p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430988ra/864501.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And as soon as it begins, it's over. Because, Maise doesn't do relationships. She never lets her true feelings get involved, never lets herself get attached.<br><br><b><i>"Yeah, I hook up with older guys. And then I leave them. Before they can leave me."</i></b><br><br>But Evan isn't a guy she can leave behind just like that. Because a few days later, on the first day of senior year, she finds out Evan is her new teacher: <b>Mr. fucking Wilke.</b><br><br>And as much as they both try to deny it, neither of them is able to pretend that one summer night not so long ago, never happened. <br><br>They're unable to deny the palpable chemistry that still runs through the air whenever they're in the same room, especially when it's a classroom...<br><br><b><i>"Our gazes struck like flint and steel. And I realized that gunsmoke smell wasn't ozone. It was us. We burned."</i></b><br><br>♦ It seems wrong, but it feels so right. ♦<br><br>It's forbidden, taboo but at the same time deliberatingly exciting.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394093i/758762.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They embark on a passionate affair with a dangerous edge to it. <br><br>Because what if all they have is based on the exhilirating feeling of forbiddenness instead of rightfulness, lust instaed of love?<br><br>♦ And what happens when everything they've been trying to keep under wraps starts spiralling out of control? ♦<br><br><b><i>Unteachable</i></b> is a story that will keep you on the edge of your seat the entire time you are reading it. I could not seem to put it down and ended up reading it in one day!<br><br>There were hot and sexy scenes as well as dramatic and emotional ones. This story was filled with <b>passion, dispair, love, lust, friendship, betrayal and hope</b>. I think the author has done an outstanding job at creating a unique, powerful story that will stay with me for a very long time and I would highly recommend everyone to give it a try. I'm already looking forward to reading much more work of this positively surprising new author!<br><br><br><b>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~</b><br><br></p><blockquote>
  <i>He touched my cheek. <b>"Who are you?"<br>"Your student."</b><br>He shook his head. <b>"No. You're the one teaching me."</b></i>
</blockquote><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430988ra/864502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430988i/864503.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
</p><blockquote>
  <i>"You should love something while you have it, love it fully and without reservation, even if you know you'll lose it someday. We lose everything. If you're trying to avoid loss, there's no point in taking another breath, or letting your heart beat one more time. It all ends." His fingers curl around mine. "That's all life is. Breathing in, breathing out. The space between two breaths."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>♡ <b>4.5 STARS.</b> ♡</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer683268383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3883827975922540559"><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/RaederUnteachableTitlebySueBee_zpsc8105448.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431420i/865743.jpg' alt=' photo RaederUnteachableTitlebySueBee_zpsc8105448.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20NIck%20Nacks/tumblr_m4j5gjeuCO1rvajq4o1_r1_500_zps1d5d8673.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380947987ra/3470612.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_m4j5gjeuCO1rvajq4o1_r1_500_zps1d5d8673.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>★★★★ 1/2! Unteachable (stand-alone). Debut by Leah Raeder. Beautifully told story about a forbidden & obsessive teacher-student romance with life lessons learned!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“No pretensions of goodness, of trying to do the right thing. We’d both wanted to embrace this fucked-up thing between us.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br/><b>Unteachable</b>, at first glance, appears to be a teacher-student romance about forbidden love… But to me it ended up being so much more than that, <b>beautifully and effortlessly told with </b></span>
  <span id="freeText3883827975922540559" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/RaederUnteachableTitlebySueBee_zpsc8105448.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431420i/865743.jpg" alt=" photo RaederUnteachableTitlebySueBee_zpsc8105448.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20NIck%20Nacks/tumblr_m4j5gjeuCO1rvajq4o1_r1_500_zps1d5d8673.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380947987ra/3470612.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m4j5gjeuCO1rvajq4o1_r1_500_zps1d5d8673.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>★★★★ 1/2! Unteachable (stand-alone). Debut by Leah Raeder. Beautifully told story about a forbidden &amp; obsessive teacher-student romance with life lessons learned!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“No pretensions of goodness, of trying to do the right thing. We’d both wanted to embrace this fucked-up thing between us.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>Unteachable</b>, at first glance, appears to be a teacher-student romance about forbidden love… But to me it ended up being so much more than that, <b>beautifully and effortlessly told with life lessons learned</b>.<br><br>Story opens up with <b>Maise O’Malley attending the carnival at the end of summer break before her senior year in high school</b>. On the roller-coaster, Deathsnake she ends up <b>sitting next to a handsome guy, Evan</b> and during those scary minutes on the rollercoaster they hit it off. They end up having <b>wild sex in Evan’s old Monte Carlo</b> and while making plans afterwards Maise tricks Evan and takes off home on her bike.<br><br>Maise has had a troubled upbringing with an absentee father and drug dealer mom. She has pretty much raised herself and somehow against-all-odds turned out to be a focused, smart and mostly mature, beyond her years, young lady. <b>She is determined not to end up like her mom and she wants to attend Film school</b>. One of her flaws, tied into her daddy-issues:<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Yeah, I hook up with older guys. And then I leave them, before they can leave me.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>Her <b>senior year in high school is going to be critical in preparation for College</b>. Imagine the shock Maise felt when she shows up for class and discovers that <b>Evan, Mr. Evan Wilke is her new Film Studies teacher</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Our gazes struck like flint and steel. And I realized that gunsmoke smell wasn’t ozone. It was us. We burned.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>Evan and Maise can’t stay away. <b>Their attraction is intense, like an obsession. Sizzling, poetic sex scenes and a brewing impossible romance</b>. She is eighteen and so in the eyes of the law it’s legal, but most likely against school policy and with a clear conflict of interest.<br><br><b>Unteachable follows Maise and Evan during her last year of high school</b>. So much is at stake as Maise needs this class for Film school. <b>It will prove to be a beyond challenging year with their insane and forbidden attraction that fuels jealousy, envy, villains, deceit, lies, blackmail and heartache</b>. <br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You should love something while you have it, love it fully and without reservation, even if you know you’ll lose it someday.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/RaederUnteachableHeroinebySueBee_zps2eb47e83.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431420i/865745.jpg" alt=" photo RaederUnteachableHeroinebySueBee_zps2eb47e83.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Six words to describe <b>Maise O’Malley: Captivating, smart, focused, strong, resilient and flawed</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“..his voice was guttural. “I can’t hold on to you. You’re like that shooting star. Just a trail of fire in my hands.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/RaederUnteachableHerobySueBee_zps18503401.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431420i/865746.jpg" alt=" photo RaederUnteachableHerobySueBee_zps18503401.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Eric Evan Wilke</b> remained a bit of an enigma throughout. Six words to describe <b>Evan: Broken, flawed, talented, immature, lovable and enigmatic</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“I saw his pupils dilating like a pulsing black heart. I saw every tremor of strain and pleasure that went through him. I watched what I did to him, how vulnerable he became as he gave himself to me…”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>Unteachable is a beautifully written story</b> and I am highly recommending! I might have wished the ending wasn’t as rushed and/or an epilogue could have followed. <b>Spellbinding storytelling! Captivating heroine! Excellent plot!</b> Thanks Ms. Raeder!<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“That’s all life is. Breathing in, breathing out. The space between two breaths.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>***<br>Hero rating: 4 stars <br>Heroine rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes frequency: 4.5 stars<br>Storyline concept rating: 4.5 stars<br>Storytelling skills rating: 5+ stars<br>Story ending rating: 3.5 stars<br>Book editing rating (5 = no edits spotted): 4.5 stars<br>************************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 4.5 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this book: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this book: Probably.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20Problems/tumblr_mbajsyPirW1ryo8vpo1_500_zps5398b012.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380431420ra/865747.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mbajsyPirW1ryo8vpo1_500_zps5398b012.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_683632685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/683632685" />
    <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash"><img alt="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391795207p2/5606933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/683632685?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash">&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17978680-unteachable">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=amethyst-words">amethyst-words</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=badass">badass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=consuming">consuming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=favorite-moments">favorite-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=holy-rusted-metal-batman">holy-rusted-metal-batman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=i-heart">i-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=insert-curse-word-here">insert-curse-word-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=intense">intense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer683632685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3407643681813728742">I fell so hard into this story, its words might as well have been made out of concrete.<br/><br/>Everyone’s talking about Leah Raeder’s writing. And they should be. Because she writes with such a red nail-polished confidence, that it’s pretty much intimate with impossible <i>not</i> to fall into it. Her writing style is effortless, interesting, and uninterested; and she writes with words that are tantamount to gunmetal and peonies.<br/><br/><b>Or something.</b> ;)<br/><br/>What’s even better than the writing itself, is that she uses its l</span>
  <span id="freeText3407643681813728742" style="display:none">I fell so hard into this story, its words might as well have been made out of concrete.<br><br>Everyone’s talking about Leah Raeder’s writing. And they should be. Because she writes with such a red nail-polished confidence, that it’s pretty much intimate with impossible <i>not</i> to fall into it. Her writing style is effortless, interesting, and uninterested; and she writes with words that are tantamount to gunmetal and peonies.<br><br><b>Or something.</b> ;)<br><br>What’s even better than the writing itself, is that she uses its lyrical beauty to describe something darkly controversial:<br><br>Teacher and student.<br>And their intensely sexual and emotional love affair.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/pin.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865827._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo pin.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She meets him at the summer carnival.<br>You know the place.<br>Where adulthood is exchanged for carousel tickets.<br><br>This is where their story begins. Because on that warm night, Maise met a boy.<br><br><b>And he was very much an adult.</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/66c29095bda3d826c1fc864729626e16.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865828.jpg" alt=" photo 66c29095bda3d826c1fc864729626e16.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now, I’m not going to tell you this is where she fell in love with him. And I’m not going to tell you that <i>this</i> was their point-of-no-return. That comes later.<br><br>Because just for now, this was just a night where just a girl met just a guy she just wanted to fuck and then she just… left.<br><br>In the moments between these events, we learn a lot about Maise.<br><br>See, on the surface; Maise is just an eighteen-year-old girl who lives with her single mom, and is approaching her senior year in highscool. But she’s actually a very diamond-faceted girl with an old soul that’s in a hurry to grow up. She only sleeps with older guys because they have the habit and emotional capacity for not getting emotionally involved.<br><br>Just like her.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/download3-9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865829._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo download3-9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then she meets Evan at the carnival. And she actually <i>likes</i> him, which freaks her out, especially when he wants to see her again after they have sex in the carnival parking lot. But that’s okay, because she never expects to see him again.<br><br>Until she comes face to face with him during the first day of school. And now, Evan, the guy she screwed in the carnival parking lot is now <b>Mr. Wilke</b>, her teacher.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/3b40a82c0b2a4bc8841c0e29f68ae543.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865830._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 3b40a82c0b2a4bc8841c0e29f68ae543.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Cue shock.<br><br>And cue the <b>hell</b> out of sexual tension. <br><br>Right away, Evan/Mr. Wilke and Maise feel that sexual attraction and overall connection they shared during that not-too-long-ago night they spent together.<br><br>And fail miserably. Because suddenly, they’re sharing heated glances in the classroom; secret caresses as they pass each other in the hallway; hotel rooms in the late afternoon; and reckless pulse-igniting trysts against the chalkboard.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/blackboard-backgrounds-wallpapers.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865831.jpg" alt=" photo blackboard-backgrounds-wallpapers.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But all too soon, they begin cutting it too close. And the ante gets higher and higher. Stolen moments turn into desperate ones. The kind of desperate moments where they silently ask:<br><br><b>Are they truly attracted to each other?<br>Or are they attracted to their clandestine secret…<br>And the thrill behind being found out?</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/53c957b6ced8e31a7498326e4109cec0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431469i/865832._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 53c957b6ced8e31a7498326e4109cec0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br> <br><br><br><br><br></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer679413302" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18122897987091794349">MINOR SPOILERS<b> -mature content reader discretion is advised.</b><br/>5 STARS out of 5<br/>Genre:NA Romance Erotica<br/>NOTE: The heroine is 18yrs of age.<br/><br/><br/><b>UNPUTDOWNABLE!</b> Some books just give it to you the way you need it. And that is <b>EXACTLY</b> what Unteachable did for me.<br/><br/><b>->The writing is addictive<br/>-->The plot line is addictive<br/>--->The characters are addictive</b><br/><br/>I just can’t get enough!<br/><br/>Maise and Evan have that <b>Reckless</b> love, that <b>Crazy</b> love, that<b> off the wall won’t stop till I had enough</b> kind of love, that<b> I don’t really ca</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18122897987091794349" style="display:none">MINOR SPOILERS<b> -mature content reader discretion is advised.</b><br>5 STARS out of 5<br>Genre:NA Romance Erotica<br>NOTE: The heroine is 18yrs of age.<br><br><br><b>UNPUTDOWNABLE!</b> Some books just give it to you the way you need it. And that is <b>EXACTLY</b> what Unteachable did for me.<br><br><b>-&gt;The writing is addictive<br>--&gt;The plot line is addictive<br>---&gt;The characters are addictive</b><br><br>I just can’t get enough!<br><br>Maise and Evan have that <b>Reckless</b> love, that <b>Crazy</b> love, that<b> off the wall won’t stop till I had enough</b> kind of love, that<b> I don’t really care we can have it anywhere</b> kind of love.(Thanks for that line Alicia Keys!)<br><br>Two people doing something they know they shouldn’t. <b>You</b> know they shouldn’t.<br>The teacher and his student, yet…<br><b>-&gt;You feel the passion every time they get together<br>--&gt;You feel the thrill of possibly being caught <br>---&gt;You feel the excitement of finally being together after a long school day/week</b><br><br>In Unteachable we meet Maise O’Malley. A young girl entering in to her senior year of high school yet has been playing the role of an adult woman since she was just a young girl. With no daddy in sight and a drug selling coke head of a mother; it’s safe to say that Maise has had a F’d up life. She may not have control of the cards life dealt her but she can however change the path she will take in the future. Which is exactly what she plans to do.<br><br><i>
  <b>‘He could have said, I’m a teacher, and everything would have been different.’</b>
</i> ~Maise<br><br>It’s August and summer is reaching its end. Maise is at the carnival drinking beer and hopping on ride after ride. The moment she decides to face her fear and get on a roller coaster called <b>Deathsnake</b>..That<b> one</b> decision changes her life.<br><br>Maise finds herself in the front row on<b> Deathsnake</b> with Evan an older guy that she not only finds attractive..*grins slyly* She also decides after spending some time with him that she wants to fuck him.(her words not mine) <br>And she does. <br>In his car. <br><br>Now this is nothing new for Maise, in fact she prefers older men. The problem with this particular man is that he actually her teacher. Neither knows of this fact <b>yet</b>. Later readers see how the forbidden aspect of this encounter jump starts a teacher-student affair.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430871i/864087.jpg" alt=" photo 7e86c6d7-e6c2-4e92-ad73-610e4cfdf532_zps4a657ba6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">	<br><br>Nothing, not one damn thing about Maise’s life is simple, it’s quite F’d up actually. She is running from the demons that have made her mother’s life a living hell. A mother she refuses to be like. A <b>doped up..drug dealing..drunken whore.</b> Could life get any worse? The answer is yes.<br><br><b>Back to school...</b><br>That moment when she goes to class and they lock eyes and she watches his realization set in seconds after hers…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430871ra/864088.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mg4wsiMBzI1qbf3wko1_500_zpscaea7564.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Worlds Collide</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430871ra/864089.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mn6a0hiR7d1ss6j2ro1_500_zps8debd912.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>‘There’s something so terrible about wanting something you’ve already had. You know exactly what you’re missing. Your body knows precisely how to shape itself around the ache, the hollowness that wants to be filled. Jesus Christ, this was only the end of the first week of school. No fucking way would I make it to winter break, let alone June.’</b>
</i> - Maise<br><br><b>Mr. Wilke</b><br>Evan Wilke is her film teacher; he is 32yrs old and in love with Maise. His love is one thing that I never questioned; I think it was obvious from the first night they met. He didn't want the night to end with her and you could feel it.<br> Evan also has a few secrets. Ha, don’t they all?!<br> <br>This teacher student affair had me enraptured from start to finish. Maise and Evan are electrifying when they are together you can't help but get zapped while reading. <br><br><b><i>“Why do I need you like this?”</i> he said, his voice rasping. I looked at his glassy, mercurial eyes, the haggard lines of want etched into his face, and said,<i> “Because you’re addicted.”</i></b><br><br><i>
  <b> ‘For an endless moment all I felt was penetration. Slow and hard. Slow and deep. He made sure I felt every single thrust.’</b>
</i> -Maise<br><br><i>
  <b>“..I want to keep you. I want to hold on and never let you go.”</b>
</i> –Evan<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430871ra/864090.gif" alt=" photo lovelustgif_zps5ee730a9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430871i/864091.jpg" alt=" photo 6c68ec79-8a00-4b64-a6d5-adcf354e8673_zpsd70e49b1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>
  <b>‘This was the inescapable truth. No matter who we were outside, in here we were teacher and student.’</b>
</i> –Maise<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430871i/864092.jpg" alt=" photo a58ba464-c9ea-413e-9109-fb0d66370bd3_zps89cf7b2f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><u>My thoughts</u><br>HOLY HELL the writing is superb the story flowed and pulled you in to this intense forbidden love affair and then BAM the author slaps you in the face with reality. With lines like <br><br><b>‘We knew what we were doing, Your Honor.’</b><br><br>SAY WHAT? Every time Maise would think of being caught readers are hit with lines that are equivalent to having cold water poured over your head. Am I the only one who felt that way while reading this??? Sheesh. I kept thinking please pleeease don’t let them get caught. I LOVE LOVE LOVED THIS BOOK! <br><br><u>
  <b>The characters</b>
</u> -Maise is a free spirit and makes no apologies for being that way. She knows what she wants and she goes after it full throttle and you will easily love that about her character. Her ability to survive and not get sucked in to the harsh world that greets her gladly on a daily basis is almost astounding. <br>And yeah she gets backed in to a corner and has to claw her way out. But that’s just it; she claws her way out and she<b> DOES NOT LOOK BACK.</b><br><b>-Evan</b> THIS MAN. I fell hard for this man. He was sweet and sexy and truly loved Maise. They each healed one another and encouraged one another in every way. Him struggling to allow Maise to live her life at 18 with or without him was heart breaking but so so sweet. If only the world had more Evan Wilke's out there.<br><br><br>My Ratings<br>Characters- Sexy, funny, lovable<br>Writing Style- EXCELLENT<br>Plot/Storyline- Teacher student romance<br>Steam Factor- HIGH/VERY <i>VERY</i> STEAMY<br>Overall- I LOVED IT!!!! READ IT!<br><b><br>Now go forth and read. Then come tell us about it on Goodreads!</b><br>For more reviews got to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogspot.com">http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogs...</a><br><br></span>

<div id="review_694057118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694057118" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694057118?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17978680-unteachable">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=indies-are-rockstars">indies-are-rockstars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-favorite">2013-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=all-the-wrong-choices">all-the-wrong-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=tough-issues">tough-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694057118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15155277725624600232">Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br/><br/><em>
  <strong>What the hell am I? I thought. Too old to be a real teenager, too young to drink. Old enough to die in a war, fuck grown men, and be completely confused about what I was doing with my life.</strong>
</em><br/><br/>One of the most important points I see argued when it comes to the classification of New Adult novels is, where does it fit? The debate seems to be evenly spit with each side categorizing it as either YA or Adult with a smaller portion claiming it is of its own category. And I get, </span>
  <span id="freeText15155277725624600232" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br><br><em>
  <strong>What the hell am I? I thought. Too old to be a real teenager, too young to drink. Old enough to die in a war, fuck grown men, and be completely confused about what I was doing with my life.</strong>
</em><br><br>One of the most important points I see argued when it comes to the classification of New Adult novels is, where does it fit? The debate seems to be evenly spit with each side categorizing it as either YA or Adult with a smaller portion claiming it is of its own category. And I get, because it is a hard to place, especially when YA itself frequently blurs the lines. In the case of <em>Unteachable</em>, however, I think the above quote really nails down what some are trying to say. There is a time in our lives when people feel neither teenaged or adult, neither fully grown or child-like. Certain privileges are afforded to you, while others remain outside your grasp. Through it all, you struggle to find a way to fit into this small space that passes by in the blink of an eye.<br><br>It would be a mistake to call Maise your average teenager, because she's far from that label with her drug dealing mom and broken home. Forced to grow up at an early age and take care of herself, she sees the world entirely differently than her classmates. But she also seeks out older male lovers to fill the void of a male figure in her life.<br><blockquote>
  <em>Thanks, Dad, for leaving a huge void in my life that Freud says has to be filled with dick. </em>
</blockquote><br>Maise is blunt, unpredictable, hot-headed, strong-willed, independent, flawed, brave, passionate and insecure all in one. After a night of of passion with a guy she meets at a carnival, she finds out that he is her new film teacher. Instead of breaking things off like she probably should have, they explore the limits of their relationship. Secret meetings away from school and make-out sessions after class make up the most of their relationship. But things get complicated when other classmates start to notice Maise's odd behavior and familiarity with their teacher and the risks the couple start to take.<br><blockquote>My face lit up with dark glee. "I can be discreet. I can be Harriet the fucking Spy."</blockquote><br>Unfortunately for Maise, she was no Harriet the Spy. And if anyone remembers what happened to poor Harriet, she got sloppy and found out by the end. The moments when Maise did a few stupid things had me shaking my head. It was fascinating to see their relationship because Maise constantly wondered what it was about Mr. Wilke that attracted her. Was is a legitimate connection between two people? Or was it just the taboo of having private after school sessions her teacher?<br><blockquote>Is falling in love with someone twice your age gross, weird, amazing, or all of the above? The secrecy insulated me in a vacuum-sealed bubble. I could only ask myself, How does this feel? Is this good? Is this right? And the only answer I ever got was my own echo.</blockquote><br>I couldn't help but wonder if Maise was even emotionally ready for such a relationship when it seemed to turn into an obsession for her. Suddenly, keeping Mr. Wilke was all she could think about, she second guessed herself more, she got desperate for his attention and jealous. But at the same time Mr. Wilke displays uncertainty of the "rightness" of his actions and struggles with his feelings for Maise.<br><blockquote>"I can't hold on to you. You're like that shooting star. Just a trail of fire in my hands."</blockquote><br>I admit to being drawn to this book simply for the taboo factor. As much as I love YA, every once in a while, it's nice to branch out to something completely left field. I mean, realistically, there is only so much pent-up sexual frustration, coupled with teenaged wangst, I can take before my head explodes. So thank goodness that <em>Unteachable</em> was around to give me the sexy times and love in such a poetic, lyrical way.<br><blockquote>Part of falling in love with someone is actually falling in love with yourself. Realizing that you're gorgeous, you're fearless, and unpredictable, you're a firecracker spitting light, entrancing a hundred faces that stare up at you with starry eyes.</blockquote><br>What I loved best about Unteachable was Raeder's prose. I love how Maise is a pretentious protagonist without actually seeming unrealistic. *Cough* <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em> *Cough* I love how hard I could relate to her feelings of not truly fitting into her world or society. I love how she could infuriate me on one page, make me laugh on another and root for her fiercely by the last. I love how Raeder's prose wrapped itself around my brain like a blanket and set off fireworks in my mind.<br><blockquote>"I'm not pulling the age card, I swear. But there's something I believe. You should love something whole you have it, love it fully and without reservations, even if you know you'll lose it someday. We lose everything. If you're trying to avoid loss, there's no point in taking another breath, or letting your heart beat one more time. It all ends." His fingers curled around mine. "That's all life is. Breathing in, breathing out. The space between two breaths."</blockquote><br>And I love how by the end of this book I cared so deeply for the characters, my feels fell out of my eyeballs.<br><br><img alt="What's happening to me?" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384277657ra/6834549.gif" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Very rarely do I see myself re-reading a book, but, guys? THIS BOOK. I would re-read the shit out of it. In fact, I would read anything Raeder wrote. <em>Unteachable</em> is a gem that gave me a bazillion happy sighs. It's lyrical, brilliantly addictive and passionate. HIGHLY recommended.<br><br>*And since <em>Unteachable</em> had so many delicious sexy time moments and it's a Kindle lending title, I'm sending it to Kat for some Cuddlebuggery Reading Time. ;)<br><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br>--------<br><br>Oh wow. This book, guys!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432950i/870924.png" alt=" photo photo_zpsd836f88d.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15155277725624600232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1776004120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1776004120" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776004120?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/19767615-henz">Henz</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=definitely-not-young-adult">definitely-not-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=psycho">psycho</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776004120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14611706424903072402"><br/>It isn’t exactly a beautiful story but I wouldn’t say it’s ugly either although I could definitely say that the writing is both which I think is quite artistic. There are many parts that are brazen, reckless even harsh, the characters exorcised the demons inside them a whole lot of times and Lolita is often used as reference (you’ll get the metaphor when you read the book ;)) but several parts [which I wished were just a tad bit more than the ugly parts ;)] are also very beautifully and thoughtf</span>
  <span id="freeText14611706424903072402" style="display:none"><br />It isn’t exactly a beautiful story but I wouldn’t say it’s ugly either although I could definitely say that the writing is both which I think is quite artistic. There are many parts that are brazen, reckless even harsh, the characters exorcised the demons inside them a whole lot of times and Lolita is often used as reference (you’ll get the metaphor when you read the book ;)) but several parts [which I wished were just a tad bit more than the ugly parts ;)] are also very beautifully and thoughtfully written. It’s a very good symbolic technique to depict life. Thus, if there’s one word that I could use to exactly describe the story, it would be realistic. <br /><br />I appreciate it when authors manage to make the readers think outside the box even if we don’t necessarily agree or approve, make us grasp life’s ambiguities and make the readers see that there is good and evil in everyone. A lot of my 2016 reads have managed to do that. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us" title="It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">It Ends With Us</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things" title="All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</a>, okay fine, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20640318.The_Girl_in_6E__Deanna_Madden___1_" title="The Girl in 6E (Deanna Madden, #1) by A.R. Torre" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl In 6E</a> and now <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20877902.Unteachable" title="Unteachable by Leah Raeder" rel="nofollow noopener">Unteachable</a>. It’s not a perfect read, there are strengths and weaknesses but it’s still generally a worthwhile read. <br /><br /><b> Just one simple advice: Keep out of children’s reach. ;) </b><br /><br />Do check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1434841712?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Henz's review</a> too for an even more positive perspective of the novel. &lt;3<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14611706424903072402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1608752299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="L A i N E Y" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y"><img alt="L A i N E Y" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546138360p2/10752235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608752299?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=you-disappoint-me">you-disappoint-me</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=ooh-chemistry">ooh-chemistry</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608752299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11719496307718369585">Oh Unteachable, what in the world happened to you?<br/><br/><i>When first we met,</i> I could not be more impressed with you and your fierce protagonist...<br/><br/>The writing was expressive and real intense. To the point that by the time half the book was gone, I started <b>to feel the weight of all the metaphors and similes</b> thown at me left and right...<br/><br/>If you like loads of metaphors/simile in your book, Raeder's writing will likely rock your world. I tend to like mine in <i>porportion,</i> totally personal preference.<br/><br/>As for the </span>
  <span id="freeText11719496307718369585" style="display:none">Oh Unteachable, what in the world happened to you?<br><br><i>When first we met,</i> I could not be more impressed with you and your fierce protagonist...<br><br>The writing was expressive and real intense. To the point that by the time half the book was gone, I started <b>to feel the weight of all the metaphors and similes</b> thown at me left and right...<br><br>If you like loads of metaphors/simile in your book, Raeder's writing will likely rock your world. I tend to like mine in <i>porportion,</i> totally personal preference.<br><br>As for the story, the MC was brilliant. <b>I love Maise</b> and I'm OK with Evan. I just didn't like the story they were in.<br><br>And it was <b>
  <i>this couple</i>
</b> that carried me to the end. When they were together there were <b>fireworks and unhealthy amount of angst.</b> <br><br>The chemistry. <br>So much chemistry. <br><br>And did I mention those smolderingly hot sexy scenes? One of the most sexually-charged scene I've ever read: I blushed like crazy reading this one scene in particular where they were in a motel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462566160ra/19015295.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book was packed full of drama, albeit the serious, somber kind, but full of drama nonetheless. That wasn't really an issue for me what <i>was</i> the issue was how they all got resolved by the end. <br><br>All of them. Poof! Gone! <br><br>Done.<br><br>Huh?<br><br>I was not expecting that, at all. I found it too neat and challenged my suspension of disbelief.<br><br>What pissed me off: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Wesley, her <i>friend,</i> semi-outed them through class project... What the hell?? Seriously, dude?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And the last scene.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435347351ra/15337545.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Again, this is a real good book. With excellent protagonist and piping-hot chemisty. Those other things just happened to push my buttons. Hence 3 stars.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
